<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="fm3035_kraft_foods_inc._and_subsidiar__kra03777"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_fm3035_1"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft Foods Inc. and Subsidiaries<BR>  Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements<BR>  (Unaudited)    <BR></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;1. Accounting Policies:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Basis of Presentation  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
interim condensed consolidated financial statements of Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. ("Kraft"), together with its subsidiaries (collectively referred to as the "Company"), are unaudited. It is the
opinion of the Company's management that all adjustments necessary for a fair statement of the interim results presented have been reflected therein. All such adjustments were of a normal recurring
nature. Net revenues and net earnings for any interim period are not necessarily indicative of results that may be expected for the entire year. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>These
statements should be read in conjunction with the Company's consolidated financial statements and related notes, and management's discussion and analysis of financial condition and results of
operations, which appear in the Company's Annual Report to Shareholders and which are incorporated by reference into the Company's Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2002 (the "2002 Form&nbsp;10-K"). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Certain
prior year amounts have been reclassified to conform with the current year's presentation, due primarily to the disclosure of more detailed information on the condensed consolidated statements
of earnings and the condensed consolidated statements of cash flows, as well as the transfer of Canadian
biscuits and pet snacks from the Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery segment to the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment, which contains the Company's other Canadian businesses. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Stock-Based Compensation Expense  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company accounts for employee stock compensation plans in accordance with the intrinsic value-based method permitted by Statement of Financial Accounting Standards ("SFAS") No.&nbsp;123,
"Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation," which did not result in compensation cost for stock options. The market value of restricted stock at date of grant is recorded as compensation expense over
the period of restriction. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, the Company granted shares of restricted stock and rights to receive shares of stock under its 2001 Performance Incentive Plan to eligible employees, giving them in
most instances all of the rights of stockholders, except that they may not sell, assign, pledge or otherwise encumber such shares and rights. Such shares and rights are subject to forfeiture if
certain employment conditions are not met. During the first quarter of 2003, the Company granted approximately 3.7&nbsp;million Class&nbsp;A shares to eligible U.S.&nbsp;&#150; based
employees and also issued to eligible non&nbsp;&#150; U.S. employees rights to receive approximately 1.6&nbsp;million Class&nbsp;A equivalent shares. Restrictions on the stock lapse in
the first quarter of 2006. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
fair value of the restricted shares and rights at the date of grant is amortized to expense ratably over the restriction period. The Company recorded compensation expense related to restricted
stock and other stock awards of $11&nbsp;million for the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2003. The unamortized portion, which is reported on the condensed consolidated balance sheets as a reduction
of earnings reinvested in the business, was $182&nbsp;million at March&nbsp;31, 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>At
March&nbsp;31, 2003, the Company had stock-based employee compensation plans. The Company applies the recognition and measurement principles of Accounting Principles Board Opinion No.&nbsp;25,
"Accounting for Stock Issued to Employees," and related Interpretations in accounting for those plans. No compensation expense for employee stock options is reflected in net earnings as all options
granted under those plans had an exercise price equal to the market value of the common stock on the date of the grant. Net earnings, as reported, includes the after-tax impact of
compensation expense related to restricted stock. The following table illustrates the effect on net earnings and earnings per share ("EPS") if the Company had applied the fair value </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>9</FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;2. Recently Adopted Accounting Standards:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Effective
January&nbsp;1, 2003, the Company adopted SFAS No.&nbsp;146, "Accounting for Costs Associated with Exit or Disposal Activities" for exit or disposal activities initiated after
December&nbsp;31, 2002. SFAS No.&nbsp;146 requires companies to recognize costs associated with exit or disposal activities when they are incurred rather than at the date of a commitment to an
exit or disposal plan. Costs covered by SFAS No.&nbsp;146 include lease termination costs and certain employee severance costs that are associated with a restructuring, discontinued operation, plant
closing or other exit or disposal activity. The adoption of SFAS No.&nbsp;146 did not have a material impact on the Company's consolidated financial position, results of operations or cash flows for
the period ended March&nbsp;31, 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Effective
January&nbsp;1, 2003, the Company adopted Financial Accounting Standards Board ("FASB") Interpretation No.&nbsp;45, "Guarantor's Accounting and Disclosure Requirements for Guarantees,
Including Indirect Guarantees of Indebtedness of Others." Interpretation No.&nbsp;45 required the disclosure of certain guarantees existing at December&nbsp;31, 2002. In addition, Interpretation
No.&nbsp;45 required the recognition of a liability for the fair value of the obligation of qualifying guarantee activities that are initiated or modified after December&nbsp;31, 2002.
Accordingly, the Company has applied the recognition provisions of Interpretation No.&nbsp;45 to guarantees initiated after December&nbsp;31, 2002. Adoption of Interpretation No.&nbsp;45 as of
January&nbsp;1, 2003 did not have a material impact on the Company's consolidated financial statements. See Note&nbsp;6. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Contingencies</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> for a further
discussion of guarantees. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
January&nbsp;2003, the FASB issued Interpretation No.&nbsp;46, "Consolidation of Variable Interest Entities." Interpretation No.&nbsp;46 requires a variable interest entity to be consolidated
by a company if that company is subject to a majority of the risk of loss from the variable interest entity's activities or is entitled to receive a majority of the entity's residual return or both.
Interpretation No.&nbsp;46 also provides criteria for determining whether an entity is a variable interest entity subject to consolidation. Interpretation No.&nbsp;46 requires immediate
consolidation of variable interest entities created after January&nbsp;31, 2003. For variable interest entities created </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>10</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;3. Related Party Transactions:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>At

Services,&nbsp;Inc., provides the Company with various services, including planning, legal, treasury, accounting, auditing, insurance, human resources, office of the secretary, corporate affairs,
information technology and tax services. Billings for these services, which were based on the cost to Altria Corporate Services,&nbsp;Inc. to provide such services and a management fee, were
$83&nbsp;million and $81&nbsp;million for the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2003 and 2002, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first three months of 2003, the Company repaid the remaining $1,150&nbsp;million to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. on the 7.0% note. In addition, at March&nbsp;31, 2003, the Company had
short-term debt totaling $2,823&nbsp;million payable to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. Interest on these borrowings is based on the applicable London Interbank Offered Rate. As noted in the
table above, a portion of the debt, totaling $1,499&nbsp;million, was reclassified on the consolidated balance sheet as long-term notes due to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. and affiliates
based upon the Company's ability and intention to refinance on a long-term basis. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;4. Acquisitions and Divestitures:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
April&nbsp;2003, the Company completed the acquisition of a biscuits business in Egypt. During the first quarter of 2002, the Company acquired a biscuits business in Australia for
$62&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2002, the Company sold several small North American food businesses which were previously classified as businesses held for sale. The aggregate proceeds received in these
transactions during the first quarter of 2002 were $81&nbsp;million. The net revenues and operating results of the businesses held for sale, which were not significant, were excluded from the
Company's condensed consolidated statements of earnings and no gain or loss was recognized on these sales. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
April&nbsp;2003, the Company announced an agreement to sell its retail rice business in Germany, Austria and Denmark. This transaction is subject to approval by the German competition
authorities. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
operating results of businesses acquired and divested were not material to the consolidated financial position or results of operations of the Company in any of the periods presented. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;6. Contingencies:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company and its subsidiaries are parties to a variety of legal proceedings arising out of the normal course of business, including a few cases in which substantial amounts of damages are sought.
While the results of litigation cannot be predicted with certainty, management believes that the final outcome
of these proceedings will not have a material adverse effect on the Company's consolidated financial position or results of operations. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Guarantees:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;At March&nbsp;31, 2003, the Company's third-party guarantees, which are primarily derived from acquisition and divestiture
activities, approximated $37&nbsp;million. Substantially all of these guarantees expire through 2012, with $26&nbsp;million expiring through March&nbsp;31, 2004. The Company is required to
perform under these guarantees in the event that a third party fails to make contractual payments or achieve performance measures. The Company has recorded a liability of $24&nbsp;million at
March&nbsp;31, 2003 relating to these guarantees. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Non-amortizable
intangible assets consist substantially of brand names purchased through the Nabisco acquisition. Amortizable intangible assets consist primarily of certain trademark
licenses and non-compete agreements. Pre-tax amortization expense for intangible assets was $2&nbsp;million for the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2003. Based upon the
amortizable intangible assets recorded in the condensed consolidated balance sheet at March&nbsp;31, 2003, amortization expense for each of the next five years is estimated to be $8&nbsp;million
or less. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
increase in goodwill and other intangible assets, net, during the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2003 of $195&nbsp;million is primarily related to currency translation. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;8. Segment Reporting:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company manufactures and markets packaged retail food products, consisting principally of beverages, cheese, snacks, convenient meals and various packaged grocery products through Kraft Foods
North America,&nbsp;Inc. ("KFNA") and Kraft Foods International,&nbsp;Inc. ("KFI"). Reportable segments for KFNA are organized and managed principally by product category. KFNA's segments are
Cheese, Meals and Enhancers; Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery; Beverages, Desserts and Cereals; and Oscar Mayer and Pizza. KFNA's food service business within the United States and its businesses in
Canada and Mexico are reported through the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment. KFI's operations are organized and managed by geographic location. KFI's segments are Europe, Middle East and Africa;
and Latin America and Asia Pacific. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's management uses operating companies income, which is defined as operating income before general corporate expenses and amortization of intangibles, to evaluate segment performance and
allocate resources. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Interest
and other debt expense, net, and provision for income taxes are centrally managed and, accordingly, such items are not presented by segment since they are not included in the measure of
segment profitability reviewed by management. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, the Company transferred management responsibility of its Canadian Biscuits and Pet Snacks operations from the Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery segment to the
Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment, which contains the Company's other Canadian businesses. Accordingly, all prior period amounts have been reclassified to reflect the transfer. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;10. Recently Issued Accounting Pronouncements:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
April&nbsp;2003, the FASB issued SFAS No.&nbsp;149, "Amendment of Statement&nbsp;133 on Derivative Instruments and Hedging Activities." SFAS No.&nbsp;149 amends and clarifies financial
accounting and reporting for derivative instruments, including certain derivative instruments embedded in other contracts and for hedging activities under SFAS No.&nbsp;133, "Accounting for
Derivative Instruments and Hedging Activities." In general, SFAS No.&nbsp;149 is effective for contracts entered into or modified after June&nbsp;30, 2003 and for hedging relationships designated
after June&nbsp;30, 2003. The Company does not currently expect the adoption of SFAS No.&nbsp;149 to have a material impact on its 2003 consolidated financial statements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
November&nbsp;2002, the Emerging Issues Task Force ("EITF") issued EITF Issue No.&nbsp;00-21, "Revenue Arrangements with Multiple Deliverables," which addresses certain aspects of
the accounting by a vendor for arrangements under which it will perform multiple revenue-generating activities. Specifically, EITF Issue No.&nbsp;00-21 addresses how to determine whether
an arrangement involving multiple deliverables contains more than one unit of accounting. EITF Issue No.&nbsp;00-21 is effective for the Company for revenue arrangements entered into
beginning July&nbsp;1, 2003. The Company does not expect the adoption of EITF Issue No.&nbsp;00-21 to have a material impact on its 2003 consolidated financial statements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="fo3035_item_2."> </A>
<A NAME="toc_fo3035_1"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Item 2.    <BR></FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="fo3035_management_s_discussion_and_an__man03466"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_fo3035_2"> </A></FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>MANAGEMENT'S DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS OF<BR>  FINANCIAL CONDITION AND RESULTS OF OPERATIONS    <BR>    </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Business Environment  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft
Foods&nbsp;Inc. ("Kraft"), together with its subsidiaries (collectively referred to as the "Company"), is the largest branded food and beverage company headquartered in the United States. At
March&nbsp;31, 2003, Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. held 97.8% of the combined voting power of the Company's outstanding capital stock and owned approximately 84.1% of the outstanding shares of the
Company's capital stock. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company conducts its global business through two subsidiaries: Kraft Foods North America,&nbsp;Inc. ("KFNA") and Kraft Foods International,&nbsp;Inc. ("KFI"). KFNA manages its operations by
product category, while KFI manages its operations by geographic region. KFNA's segments are Cheese, Meals and Enhancers; Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery; Beverages, Desserts and Cereals; and Oscar
Mayer and Pizza. KFNA's food service business within the United States and its businesses in Canada and Mexico are reported through the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment. KFI's segments are Europe,
Middle East and Africa; and Latin America and Asia Pacific. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company is subject to fluctuating commodity costs, currency movements and competitive challenges in various product categories and markets, including a trend toward increasing consolidation in the
retail trade and consequent inventory reductions, and changing consumer preferences. In addition, certain competitors may have different profit objectives, and some competitors may be more or less
susceptible to currency exchange rates. To confront these challenges, the Company continues to
take steps to build the value of its brands and improve its food business portfolio with new products and marketing initiatives. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Fluctuations
in commodity prices can lead to retail price volatility, intensify price competition and influence consumer and trade buying patterns. KFNA's and KFI's businesses are subject to
fluctuating commodity costs, including dairy, coffee bean and cocoa costs. Dairy commodity prices in the first quarter of 2003 on average were lower than those incurred in the first quarter of 2002,
while cocoa bean prices increased significantly and coffee bean prices were also higher than in the first quarter of 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>On
December&nbsp;11, 2000, the Company acquired all of the outstanding shares of Nabisco Holdings Corp. ("Nabisco"). The closure of a number of Nabisco domestic and international facilities resulted
in severance and other exit costs of $379&nbsp;million, which were included in the adjustments for the allocation of the Nabisco purchase price. The closures will result in the termination of
approximately 7,500 employees and will require total cash payments of $373&nbsp;million, of which approximately $200&nbsp;million has been spent through March&nbsp;31, 2003. Substantially all of
the closures were completed as of December&nbsp;31, 2002, and the remaining payments relate to salary continuation payments for severed employees and lease payments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
integration of Nabisco into the operations of the Company has also resulted in the closure or reconfiguration of several of the Company's existing facilities. During the first quarter of 2002,
approximately 700 salaried employees elected to retire or terminate employment under voluntary retirement programs. As a result, the Company recorded a pre-tax charge of
$142&nbsp;million during the first quarter of 2002 related to these programs. In addition, during the first quarter of 2002, the Company recorded pre-tax integration related charges of
$27&nbsp;million to consolidate production lines in North America. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>16</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=16,EFW="2110635",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=176400,FOLIO='16',FILE='DISK016:[03CHI5.03CHI3035]FO3035A.;7',USER='ABLIJDE',CD='14-MAY-2003;14:14' -->
<A NAME="page_fo3035_1_17"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>As
more fully discussed in the Debt and Liquidity section, during the first quarter of 2003, as a result of a judgment against Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc.'s domestic tobacco subsidiary, the Company's
credit ratings were lowered with the resultant effect of eliminating access to the commercial paper market. As a result, in April&nbsp;2003, the Company began to borrow on its revolving credit
agreements, having the impact of increasing borrowing costs. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
April&nbsp;2003, the Company completed the acquisition of a biscuits business in Egypt. During the first quarter of 2002, the Company acquired a biscuits business in Australia for
$62&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2002, the Company sold several small North American food businesses which were previously classified as businesses held for sale. The aggregate proceeds received in these
transactions during the first quarter of 2002 were $81&nbsp;million. The net revenues and operating results of the businesses held for sale, which were not significant, were excluded from the
Company's condensed consolidated statements of earnings and no gain or loss was recognized on these sales. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
April&nbsp;2003, the Company announced an agreement to sell its retail rice business in Germany, Austria and Denmark. This transaction is subject to approval by the German competition
authorities. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
operating results of businesses acquired and divested were not material to the consolidated financial position or results of operations of the Company in any of the periods presented. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
for the first quarter of 2003 increased 0.1% over the comparable 2002 period due primarily to increased shipments in the Beverages, Desserts&nbsp;&amp; Cereals segment, aided by new product
introductions, partially offset by the shift in shipments supporting the Easter holiday, which falls into the second quarter of 2003 versus the first quarter of 2002, a reduction in trade inventories,
the impact of divested businesses and a national strike in Venezuela. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues for the first quarter of 2003 increased $212&nbsp;million (3.0%) over the comparable 2002 period due primarily to higher pricing ($116&nbsp;million, driven by higher commodity and
currency devaluation-driven costs), favorable currency movements ($81&nbsp;million) and higher volume/mix ($28&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of 2002 divested businesses
($22&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
income for the first quarter of 2003 increased $184&nbsp;million (14.1%) over the comparable 2002 period, due primarily to the 2002 pre-tax charges for separation programs
($142&nbsp;million) and integration costs ($27&nbsp;million), higher pricing, net of cost increases ($104&nbsp;million, including productivity and synergy savings) and favorable currency
movements ($6&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher marketing, administration and research costs ($52&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs) and unfavorable volume/mix
($34&nbsp;million). The higher benefit costs were primarily related to pensions and stock compensation costs relating to the issuance of restricted stock awards to employees. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>As
discussed in Note&nbsp;8. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Segment Reporting</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, management reviews operating companies income, which is defined as operating income before corporate
expenses and amortization of intangibles, to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. Management believes it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help investors analyze business
performance and trends. Operating companies income increased $184&nbsp;million (13.6%) over the first quarter of 2002, due to the same factors discussed above for operating income. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Currency
movements have increased net revenues by $81&nbsp;million and operating companies income by $6&nbsp;million over the first quarter of 2002. These increases in net revenues and operating
companies income are due primarily to the weakness of the U.S. dollar against the euro and other currencies, partially offset by the strength of the U.S. dollar against certain Latin American
currencies. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Interest
and other debt expense, net, decreased $51&nbsp;million from the first quarter of 2002. This decrease is due to the Company's refinancing of notes payable to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc.,
lower short-term interest rates and the use of free cash flow to pay down debt. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
earnings of $848&nbsp;million for the first quarter of 2003 increased $155&nbsp;million (22.4%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to growth in operating companies income and
lower interest expense. Diluted and basic earnings per share ("EPS"), which were both $0.49 for the first quarter of 2003, increased by 22.5% over 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, the Company transferred management responsibility of its Canadian Biscuits and Pet Snacks operations from the Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery segment to the
Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment, which contains the Company's other Canadian businesses. Accordingly, all prior period amounts have been reclassified to reflect the transfer. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
for the first quarter of 2003 increased 1.3% over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to new products and increased shipments in the Beverages, Desserts and Cereals and Oscar Mayer and
Pizza segments, partially offset by the shift in Easter timing and trade inventory reductions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, net revenues increased $86&nbsp;million (1.6%) over the first quarter of 2002, due primarily to higher volume/mix ($53&nbsp;million) and higher pricing
($43&nbsp;million), partially offset by unfavorable currency movements and the divestiture of a small confectionery business in 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the first quarter of 2003 increased $199&nbsp;million (18.1%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to the absence of the 2002 pre-tax charges
for separation programs ($135&nbsp;million) and integration costs ($27&nbsp;million), and higher pricing, net of cost increases on certain businesses, lower cheese commodity costs and productivity
and synergy savings ($87&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher marketing, administration and research costs ($27&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs) and unfavorable volume/mix. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>19</FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="page_fq3035_1_20"> </A> </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2>
The following discusses operating results within each of KFNA's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> Cheese, Meals and Enhancers.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume in the first quarter of 2003 decreased 0.4% from the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to the shift in Easter timing and
lower trade inventories, which particularly impacted the cheese and enhancers businesses. Volume in Canada and Mexico increased, driven by new product introductions in beverages. Volume in the food
service business in the United States also increased due to higher shipments to national accounts. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, net revenues decreased $29&nbsp;million (1.3%) from the first quarter of 2002, due to lower volume/mix ($35&nbsp;million) and unfavorable currency movements
($6&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher pricing ($12&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the first quarter of 2003 increased $86&nbsp;million (18.7%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to the 2002 pre-tax charges for separation
programs ($60&nbsp;million) and integration costs ($27&nbsp;million), higher pricing in certain businesses and lower cheese commodity costs and productivity savings ($50&nbsp;million), partially
offset by lower volume/mix ($35&nbsp;million) and higher benefit costs. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume in the first quarter of 2003 decreased 1.8% from the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to trade inventory
reductions, a planned shift to lower-weight, higher-revenue-per-pound new products and a 2002 confectionery divestiture. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, net revenues increased $47&nbsp;million (4.3%) over the first quarter of 2002, due primarily to higher volume/mix ($42&nbsp;million) and higher pricing
($9&nbsp;million), partially offset by a 2002 divested confectionery business. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the first quarter of 2003 increased $20&nbsp;million (10.3%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to higher pricing and favorable costs
($25&nbsp;million), higher volume/mix ($8&nbsp;million) and synergy savings, partially offset by higher marketing, administration and research costs. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> Beverages, Desserts and Cereals.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume in the first quarter of 2003 increased 5.1% over the comparable period in 2002, due primarily to higher shipments of
ready-to-drink beverages and cereals, which were aided by new product introductions. Volume declined in coffee, dry packaged desserts and frozen whipped toppings due primarily
to the shift in the timing of Easter. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, net revenues increased $34&nbsp;million (2.9%) over the first quarter of 2002, due to higher volume/mix ($19&nbsp;million) and higher pricing
($15&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the first quarter of 2003 increased $67&nbsp;million (21.8%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to the 2002 pre-tax charge for separation
programs ($47&nbsp;million), lower marketing, administration and research costs ($18&nbsp;million) and higher volume/mix, partially offset by higher benefit costs. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> Oscar Mayer and Pizza.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume in the first quarter of 2003 increased 2.3% over the comparable period of 2002, due to volume gains in frozen pizza, bacon, hot dogs,
lunch combinations and soy-based meat alternatives. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, net revenues increased $34&nbsp;million (4.5%) over the first quarter of 2002 due primarily to higher volume/mix ($27&nbsp;million) and higher pricing. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the first quarter of 2003 increased $26&nbsp;million (19.4%) over the comparable period of 2002 due to the 2002 pre-tax charge for separation programs
($25&nbsp;million), and higher </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>volume/mix
($11&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher marketing, administration and research costs ($10&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
for the first quarter of 2003 decreased 3.2% from the first quarter of 2002, due primarily to the divestiture of a Latin American bakery ingredients business in 2002 and lower volume due to the
national strike in Venezuela and the shift in Easter shipments. This decrease in volume was partially offset by new product introductions, the impact of marketing programs and by the 2002 acquisition
of a snacks business in Turkey. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, net revenues increased $126&nbsp;million (6.8%) over the first quarter of 2002, due primarily to favorable currency movements ($87&nbsp;million), higher pricing
($73&nbsp;million, due primarily to higher commodity and currency devaluation-driven costs) and the 2002 acquisition of a snacks business in Turkey, partially offset by lower volume/mix
($25&nbsp;million) and the impact of divestitures ($18&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the first quarter of 2003 decreased $15&nbsp;million (6.0%) from the first quarter of 2002, due primarily to higher marketing, administration and research costs
($25&nbsp;million) and lower volume/mix ($21&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher pricing, net of cost increases ($17&nbsp;million), the absence of a 2002 pre-tax charge for
separation programs ($7&nbsp;million) and favorable currency movements ($7&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of KFI's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> Europe, Middle East and Africa.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume for the first quarter of 2003 increased 1.1% over the comparable period of 2002, driven by volume growth across the Central
and Eastern Europe, Middle East and Africa region, new product introductions and the acquisition of a snacks business in Turkey in the third quarter of 2002, partially offset by the shift in Easter
shipments and price competition in select markets impacting the European Union region. Snacks volume increased, benefiting from the 2002 acquisition in Turkey and the continued growth of confectionery
businesses in Russia and Poland, partially offset by the shift in Easter shipments. Beverages volume also increased, due primarily to increased coffee
shipments in most markets, including France, Germany, Italy, Poland and Russia. Cheese volume was comparable with prior year, as gains in cream cheese and cheese slices in Italy were offset by lower
volume in Germany and Iberia due to increased </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>21</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=2,SEQ=21,EFW="2110635",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=142487,FOLIO='21',FILE='DISK016:[03CHI5.03CHI3035]FQ3035A.;19',USER='ABLIJDE',CD='14-MAY-2003;14:14' -->
<A NAME="page_fq3035_1_22"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>price
competition. In convenient meals, volume was also comparable to prior year as higher shipments of canned meats in Italy were offset primarily by declines in Germany. In grocery, volume declined
due primarily to lower sales in the European Union. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues for the first quarter of 2003 increased $209&nbsp;million (15.5%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to favorable currency movements ($205&nbsp;million), the 2002
acquisition of a snacks business in Turkey and higher volume/mix, partially offset by lower pricing ($11&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the first quarter of 2003 increased $21&nbsp;million (12.0%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to favorable currency movements ($21&nbsp;million),
lower marketing and administration costs and the absence of a 2002 pre-tax charge for separation programs, partially offset by lower pricing and cost increases ($16&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> Latin America and Asia Pacific.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume for the first quarter of 2003 decreased 9.2% from the comparable period in 2002, due primarily to the divestiture of a Latin
American bakery ingredients business in 2002, the national strike in Venezuela and the shift in Easter shipments, partially offset by growth in most Asia Pacific markets. Snacks volume decreased, due
primarily to the national strike in Venezuela and the shift in Easter shipments, partially offset by biscuits volume growth in many markets, including Brazil, Central America, Australia, Southeast
Asia and China. In grocery, volume declined in Latin America, due to the sale of a Latin American bakery ingredients business in the fourth quarter of 2002. In beverages, volume increased in both
coffee and refreshment beverages. Coffee volume increased, due primarily to increased shipments to China and Australia. Refreshment beverages volume increased, due primarily to growth in most markets,
including Brazil, Argentina, Venezuela and the Philippines, aided by new product introductions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, net revenues decreased $83&nbsp;million (16.3%) from the first quarter of 2002, due to unfavorable currency movements ($118&nbsp;million), lower volume/mix
($31&nbsp;million) and the divestiture of a Latin American bakery ingredients business in 2002 ($18&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher pricing ($84&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the first quarter of 2003 decreased $36&nbsp;million (46.8%) from the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to higher marketing, administration and research costs
($34&nbsp;million), lower volume/mix ($21&nbsp;million) and unfavorable currency movements ($14&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher pricing, net of cost increases ($33&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Financial Review</U>  </B></FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Net Cash Provided by Operating Activities</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, net cash provided by operating activities was $315&nbsp;million compared with $216&nbsp;million in the comparable 2002 period. The increase in net cash provided
by operating activities is due primarily to a lower use of cash to satisfy amounts due to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc., and higher net earnings, primarily related to the absence of prior year separation
and integration programs, partially offset by higher levels of cash used to fund an increase in working capital. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Net Cash Used in Investing Activities</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>One
element of the growth strategy of the Company is to strengthen its brand portfolios through disciplined programs of selective acquisitions and divestitures. The Company is constantly investigating
potential acquisition candidates and from time to time sells businesses that are outside its core categories or that do not meet its growth or profitability targets. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, net cash used in investing activities was $222&nbsp;million, compared with $171&nbsp;million in the first quarter of 2002. This increase primarily reflects the
absence of cash received from the 2002 </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>22</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=22,EFW="2110635",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=633969,FOLIO='22',FILE='DISK016:[03CHI5.03CHI3035]FQ3035A.;19',USER='ABLIJDE',CD='14-MAY-2003;14:14' -->
<A NAME="page_fq3035_1_23"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>divestiture
of several North American food businesses and an increase in capital expenditures, partially offset by lower purchases of businesses. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Net Cash Used in Financing Activities</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, net cash used in financing activities was $140&nbsp;million, compared with $54&nbsp;million during the first quarter of 2002. The increase in cash used was due
primarily to the Company's repurchases of Class&nbsp;A common stock and higher dividends paid, reflecting a higher dividend rate in 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Debt and Liquidity</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I> Debt.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company's total debt, including amounts due to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. and affiliates, was $14.7&nbsp;billion at March&nbsp;31, 2003 and
$14.4&nbsp;billion at December&nbsp;31, 2002. An increase in third-party borrowings was partially offset by a decrease in debt due to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. and affiliates. The Company's
debt-to-equity ratio was 0.56 at March&nbsp;31, 2003 and December&nbsp;31, 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, the Company repaid the remaining $1,150&nbsp;million of the 7.0% long-term notes payable to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. and affiliates. In addition, at
March&nbsp;31, 2003, the Company had short-term debt totaling $2,823&nbsp;million payable to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. and affiliates. Interest on these borrowings is based on the
applicable London Interbank Offered Rate. A portion of the short-term debt, totaling $1,499&nbsp;million, was reclassified on the consolidated balance sheet as long-term
notes due to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. and affiliates based upon the Company's ability and intention to refinance on a long-term basis. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I> Credit Ratings.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Following a $10.1&nbsp;billion judgment on March&nbsp;21, 2003 against Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc.'s domestic tobacco subsidiary, Philip Morris
USA&nbsp;Inc., the three major credit rating agencies took a series of ratings actions resulting in the lowering of the Company's short-term and long-term debt ratings,
despite the fact the Company is not a party to, nor has exposure to this litigation. Between March&nbsp;21, 2003 and early May&nbsp;2003, Moody's lowered the Company's
short-term debt rating from "P-1" to "P-2" and its long-term debt rating from "A2" to "A3" with stable outlook. Standard&nbsp;&amp; Poor's lowered the
Company's short-term debt rating from "A-1" to "A-2" and its long-term debt rating from "A-" to "BBB+" while maintaining these ratings on
credit watch with negative implications. Fitch Rating Services lowered the Company's short-term debt rating from "F-1" to "F-2" and its long-term debt
rating from "A" to "BBB", with stable outlook. As a result of the credit rating agencies' actions, borrowing costs for the Company have increased. None of the Company's debt agreements requires
accelerated repayment in the event of a decrease in credit ratings. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>23</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I> Credit Lines.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company maintains revolving credit facilities that have historically been used to support the issuance of commercial paper. However, as a result
of the recent rating agencies' actions, the Company's access to the commercial paper market was eliminated. Subsequently, in April&nbsp;2003, the Company began to borrow against existing credit
facilities to repay maturing commercial paper and to fund normal working capital needs. At March&nbsp;31, 2003 and at May&nbsp;6, 2003, credit lines for the Company and the related activity were
as follows (in billions of dollars): </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Information
has been provided as of May&nbsp;6, 2003 to provide investors with additional information about changes in the Company's debt structure subsequent to March&nbsp;31, 2003. To meet
maturing commercial paper obligations, the Company had $0.5&nbsp;billion of cash invested in short-term money market instruments as of May&nbsp;6, 2003. In addition, as of
May&nbsp;6, 2003, commercial paper outstanding included $0.1&nbsp;billion of short-term borrowings that were obtained in the commercial paper market subsequent to recent actions by the
rating agencies. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's credit facilities, which are for the sole use of the Company, require the maintenance of a minimum net worth. The Company met this covenant at March&nbsp;31, 2003. The foregoing
revolving credit facilities do not include any other financial tests, any credit rating triggers or any provisions that could require the posting of collateral. The 364-day facility
expires in July&nbsp;2003 while the multi-year facility expires in July&nbsp;2006. The Company will begin negotiating a new 364-day facility during the second quarter of
2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
addition to the above, certain international subsidiaries of the Company maintain uncommitted credit lines to meet the short-term working capital needs of the international businesses.
These credit lines, which amounted to approximately $0.6&nbsp;billion as of March&nbsp;31, 2003, are for the sole use of the Company's international businesses. At March&nbsp;31, 2003,
borrowings on these lines amounted to approximately $0.2&nbsp;billion. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I> Guarantees.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As discussed in Note&nbsp;6. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Contingencies</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, the Company had third-party guarantees, which are
primarily derived from acquisition and divestiture activities, of approximately $37&nbsp;million at March&nbsp;31, 2003. Substantially all of these guarantees expire through 2012, with
$26&nbsp;million expiring through March&nbsp;31, 2004. The Company is required to perform under these guarantees in the event that a third party fails to make contractual payments or achieve
performance measures. The Company has recorded a liability of $24&nbsp;million at March&nbsp;31, 2003 relating to these guarantees. In addition, at March&nbsp;31, 2003, the Company was
contingently liable for $108&nbsp;million of guarantees related to its own performance. These include surety bonds related to dairy commodity purchases and guarantees related to letters of credit
and taxes. Guarantees do not have, and are not expected to have, a significant impact on the Company's liquidity. </FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE ALIGN="CENTER" WIDTH="120">

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company believes that its cash from operations and existing credit facilities will provide sufficient liquidity to meet its working capital needs, planned capital expenditures and payment of its
anticipated quarterly dividends. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>24</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="page_fs3035_1_25"> </A> </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><U>Equity and Dividends</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company repurchased 2.7&nbsp;million shares of its Class&nbsp;A common stock during the first quarter of 2003 at a cost of $82.5&nbsp;million. At March&nbsp;31, 2003, cumulative
repurchases under its previously announced $500&nbsp;million authority totaled 7.1&nbsp;million shares of Class&nbsp;A common stock at an aggregate cost of $252.5&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, the Company granted shares of restricted stock and rights to receive shares of stock under its 2001 Performance Incentive Plan to eligible employees, giving them in
most instances all of the rights of stockholders, except that they may not sell, assign, pledge or otherwise encumber such shares and rights. Such shares and rights are subject to forfeiture if
certain employment conditions are not met. During the first quarter of 2003, the Company granted approximately 3.7&nbsp;million Class&nbsp;A shares to eligible U.S.&nbsp;- based employees and
also issued to eligible non&nbsp;- U.S. employees rights to receive approximately 1.6&nbsp;million Class&nbsp;A equivalent shares. Restrictions on the stock lapse in the first quarter of 2006. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
fair value of the restricted shares and rights at the date of grant is amortized to expense ratably over the restriction period. The Company recorded compensation expense related to restricted
stock and other stock awards of $11&nbsp;million for the quarter ended March&nbsp;31, 2003. The unamortized portion, which is reported on the condensed consolidated balance sheets as a reduction
of earnings reinvested in the business, was $182&nbsp;million at March&nbsp;31, 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Dividends
paid in the first quarter of 2003 and 2002 were $259&nbsp;million and $225&nbsp;million, respectively, an increase of 15.1%, reflecting a higher dividend rate in 2003, partially offset
by a lower number of shares outstanding as a result of share repurchases. The present annualized dividend rate is $0.60 per common share. The declaration of dividends is subject to the discretion of
the Company's Board of Directors and will depend on various factors, including the Company's net earnings, financial condition, cash requirements, future prospects and other factors deemed relevant by
the Company's Board of Directors. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Market Risk</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company operates globally, with manufacturing and sales facilities in various locations around the world, and utilizes certain financial instruments to manage its foreign currency and commodity
exposures, which primarily relate to forecasted transactions. Derivative financial instruments are used by the Company, principally to reduce exposures to market risks resulting from fluctuations in
foreign exchange rates and commodity prices by creating offsetting exposures. The Company is not a party to leveraged derivatives and, by policy, does not use financial instruments for speculative
purposes. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Substantially
all of the Company's derivative financial instruments are effective as hedges under Statement of Financial Accounting Standards ("SFAS") No.&nbsp;133, "Accounting for Derivative
Instruments and Hedging Activities." During the quarters ended March&nbsp;31, 2003 and 2002, ineffectiveness related to cash flow hedges was not material. At March&nbsp;31, 2003, the Company was
hedging forecasted transactions for periods not exceeding twenty months and expects substantially all amounts reported in accumulated other comprehensive earnings (losses) to be reclassified to the
consolidated statement of earnings within the next twelve months. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> Foreign exchange rates.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company uses forward foreign exchange contracts and foreign currency options to mitigate its exposure to changes in foreign currency
exchange rates from third-party and intercompany forecasted transactions. The primary currencies to which the Company is exposed, based on the size and location of its operations, include the euro,
British pound and Canadian dollar. At March&nbsp;31, 2003 and December&nbsp;31, 2002, the Company had option and forward foreign exchange contracts with aggregate notional amounts of
$877&nbsp;million and $575&nbsp;million, respectively, which are comprised of contracts for the purchase and sale of foreign currencies. The effective portion of unrealized gains and losses
associated with forward contracts is deferred as a component of accumulated other comprehensive earnings (losses) until the underlying hedged transactions are reported on the Company's consolidated
statement of earnings. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>25</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=25,EFW="2110635",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=393029,FOLIO='25',FILE='DISK016:[03CHI5.03CHI3035]FS3035A.;7',USER='ABLIJDE',CD='14-MAY-2003;14:14' -->
<A NAME="page_fs3035_1_26"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> Commodities.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company is exposed to price risk related to forecasted purchases of certain commodities used as raw materials by the Company's businesses.
Accordingly, the Company uses commodity forward contracts, as cash flow hedges, primarily for coffee, cocoa, milk and cheese.
Commodity futures and options are also used to hedge the price of certain commodities, including milk, coffee, cocoa, wheat, corn, sugar and soybean oil. In general, commodity forward contracts
qualify for the normal purchase exception under SFAS No.&nbsp;133 and are, therefore, not subject to the provisions of SFAS No.&nbsp;133. At March&nbsp;31, 2003 and December&nbsp;31, 2002, the
Company had net long commodity positions of $773&nbsp;million and $544&nbsp;million, respectively. Unrealized gains or losses on net commodity positions were immaterial at March&nbsp;31, 2003
and December&nbsp;31, 2002. The effective portion of unrealized gains and losses on commodity futures and option contracts is deferred as a component of accumulated other comprehensive earnings
(losses) and is recognized as a component of cost of sales in the Company's consolidated statement of earnings when the related inventory is sold. </FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE ALIGN="CENTER" WIDTH="120">

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Use
of the above-mentioned derivative financial instruments has not had a material impact on the Company's financial position at March&nbsp;31, 2003 and December&nbsp;31, 2002, or the Company's
results of operations for the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2003 or the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002. </FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE ALIGN="CENTER" WIDTH="120">

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Contingencies</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>See
Note&nbsp;6. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Contingencies</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> and Part&nbsp;II&nbsp;&#150; Other Information, Item&nbsp;1. Legal Proceedings for a discussion of
contingencies. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>New Accounting Standards</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
April&nbsp;2003, the Financial Accounting Standards Board ("FASB") issued SFAS No.&nbsp;149, "Amendment of Statement&nbsp;133 on Derivative Instruments and Hedging Activities." SFAS
No.&nbsp;149 amends and clarifies financial accounting and reporting for derivative instruments, including certain derivative instruments embedded in other contracts and for hedging activities under
SFAS No.&nbsp;133, "Accounting for Derivative Instruments and Hedging Activities." In general, SFAS No.&nbsp;149 is effective for contracts entered into or modified after June&nbsp;30, 2003 and
for hedging relationships designated after June&nbsp;30, 2003. The Company does not currently expect the adoption of SFAS No.&nbsp;149 to have a material impact on its 2003 consolidated financial
statements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Effective
January&nbsp;1, 2003, the Company adopted SFAS No.&nbsp;146, "Accounting for Costs Associated with Exit or Disposal Activities" for exit or disposal activities initiated after
December&nbsp;31, 2002. SFAS No.&nbsp;146 requires companies to recognize costs associated with exit or disposal activities when they are incurred rather than at the date of a commitment to an
exit or disposal plan. Costs covered by SFAS No.&nbsp;146 include lease termination costs and certain employee severance costs that are associated with a restructuring, discontinued operation, plant
closing or other exit or disposal activity. The adoption of SFAS No.&nbsp;146 did not have a material impact on the Company's consolidated financial position, results of operations or cash flows for
the period ended March&nbsp;31, 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Effective
January&nbsp;1, 2003, the Company adopted FASB Interpretation No.&nbsp;45, "Guarantor's Accounting and Disclosure Requirements for Guarantees, Including Indirect Guarantees of
Indebtedness of Others." Interpretation No.&nbsp;45 required the disclosure of certain guarantees existing at December&nbsp;31, 2002. In addition, Interpretation No.&nbsp;45 required the
recognition of a liability for the fair value of the obligation of qualifying guarantee activities that are initiated or modified after December&nbsp;31, 2002. Accordingly, the Company has applied
the recognition provisions of Interpretation No.&nbsp;45 to guarantees initiated after December&nbsp;31, 2002. Adoption of Interpretation No.&nbsp;45 as of January&nbsp;1, 2003 did not have a
material impact on the Company's consolidated financial statements. See Note&nbsp;6. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Contingencies</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> for a further discussion of guarantees. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
January&nbsp;2003, the FASB issued Interpretation No.&nbsp;46, "Consolidation of Variable Interest Entities." Interpretation No.&nbsp;46 requires a variable interest entity to be consolidated
by a company if that company is subject to a majority of the risk of loss from the variable interest entity's activities or is entitled to receive a majority of the entity's residual return or both.
Interpretation No.&nbsp;46 also provides criteria for determining whether an entity is a variable interest entity subject to consolidation. Interpretation No.&nbsp;46 requires immediate
consolidation of variable interest entities created after January&nbsp;31, 2003. For variable interest entities created prior to February&nbsp;1, 2003, consolidation is required on July&nbsp;1,
2003. The adoption of Interpretation No.&nbsp;46 on January&nbsp;1, 2003 did not have a material impact on the Company's consolidated financial statements. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>26</FONT></P>

<A NAME="page_fs3035_1_27"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
November&nbsp;2002, the Emerging Issues Task Force ("EITF") issued EITF Issue No.&nbsp;00-21, "Revenue Arrangements with Multiple Deliverables," which addresses certain aspects of
the accounting by a vendor for arrangements under which it will perform multiple revenue-generating activities. Specifically, EITF Issue No.&nbsp;00-21 addresses how to determine whether
an arrangement involving multiple deliverables contains more than one unit of accounting. EITF Issue No.&nbsp;00-21 is effective for the Company for revenue arrangements entered into
beginning July&nbsp;1, 2003. The Company does not expect the adoption of EITF Issue No.&nbsp;00-21 to have a material impact on its 2003 consolidated financial statements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Forward-Looking and Cautionary Statements</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company and its representatives may from time to time make written or oral forward-looking statements, including statements contained in the Company's filings with the SEC and in its reports to
shareholders. One can identify these forward-looking statements by use of words such as "strategy," "expects," "plans," "anticipates," "believes," "will," "continues," "estimates," "intends,"
"projects," "goals," "targets" and other words of similar meaning. One can also identify them by the fact that they do not relate strictly to historical or current facts. These statements are based on
our assumptions and estimates and are subject to risks and uncertainties. In connection with the "safe harbor" provisions of the Private Securities Litigation Reform Act of 1995, the Company is hereby
identifying important factors that could cause actual results and outcomes to differ materially from those contained in any forward-looking statement made by or on behalf of the Company; any such
statement is qualified by reference to the following cautionary statements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Each
of the Company's segments is subject to intense competition, changes in consumer preferences, demand for its products, the effects of changing prices for its raw materials and local economic and
market conditions. Their results are dependent upon their continued ability to promote brand equity successfully, to anticipate and respond to new consumer trends, to develop new products and markets,
to broaden brand portfolios in order to compete effectively with lower priced products in a consolidating environment at the retail and manufacturing levels, to improve productivity and to maintain
access to credit markets. The Company's results are also dependent on its ability to consummate and successfully integrate acquisitions, including its ability to derive cost savings from the
integration of Nabisco's operations with the Company. In addition, the Company is subject to the effects of foreign economies, currency movements, fluctuations in levels of customer inventories and
credit and other business risks related to its customers operating in a challenging economic and competitive environment. The Company's results are dependent upon its borrowing costs and credit
ratings, which may in turn be influenced by the credit ratings of Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. The Company's benefit expense is subject to the investment performance of pension plan assets, interest
rates and cost increases for medical benefits offered to employees and retirees. The food industry continues to be subject to recalls if products become adulterated or misbranded, liability if product
consumption causes injury, ingredient disclosure and labeling laws and regulations and the possibility that consumers could lose confidence in the safety and quality of certain food products.
Developments in any of these areas, which are more fully described elsewhere in this document and which descriptions are incorporated into this section by reference, could cause the Company's results
to differ materially from results that have been or may be projected by or on behalf of the Company. The Company cautions that the foregoing list of important factors is not exclusive. Any
forward-looking statements are made as of the date of the document in which they appear. The Company does not undertake to update any forward-looking statement that may be made from time to time by or
on behalf of the Company. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><A

<A NAME="toc_fu3035_1"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Item 4. Controls and Procedures    <BR></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Within
the 90&nbsp;days prior to the filing date of this report, the Company carried out an evaluation, under the supervision and with the participation of the Company's management, including the
Company's Chairman, Co-Chief Executive Officers, and Chief Financial Officer, of the effectiveness of the design and operation of the Company's disclosure controls and procedures pursuant
to Rule&nbsp;13a-14 under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934. Based upon that evaluation, the Chairman, Co-Chief Executive Officers, and Chief Financial Officer concluded
that the Company's disclosure controls and procedures are effective in timely alerting them to material information relating to the Company (including its consolidated subsidiaries) required to be
included in the Company's periodic SEC filings. Since the date of the evaluation, there have been no significant changes in the Company's internal controls or in other factors that could significantly
affect the controls. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="fw3035_part_ii__#150;_other_information"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_fw3035_1"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Part&nbsp;II &#150; OTHER INFORMATION    <BR></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="fw3035_item_1._legal_proceedings."> </A>
<A NAME="toc_fw3035_2"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Item 1. Legal Proceedings.    <BR></FONT></P>

<UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Legal Proceedings</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company is party to a variety of legal proceedings arising out of the normal course of business, including the matters discussed below. While the results of litigation cannot be predicted with
certainty, management believes that the final outcome of these proceedings will not have a material adverse effect on the Company's results of operations or financial position. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>On
May 5, 2003, a complaint was filed under Sections 17200 and 17203 of the California Business and Professions Code against the Company in California Superior Court, County of Marin, by
BanTransFats.com, Inc. The complaint seeks an injunction against, among other things, the marketing and selling of Oreo cookies to children in the State of California until such cookies contain no
partially hydrogenated oil or other trans fat. The complaint alleges, among other things, that hydrogenated and partially hydrogenated oils are "toxic" and "unsafe and unfit for human consumption."
Although the Company has not yet been officially served with the complaint, the Company has reviewed a copy of the complaint, believes that the suit is unwarranted and will vigorously defend the
litigation. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
May&nbsp;2002, the Company was served with a lawsuit filed in California by the American Environmental Safety Institute against several major chocolate manufacturers alleging that the defendants'
chocolate products contain "potentially dangerous levels of lead and cadmium." The suit alleges that these levels, which are not disclosed on the product labels, are a violation of California's </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><I>Proposition 65</I></FONT><FONT
SIZE=2>, which requires a warning on products containing chemicals "known to the State" to be carcinogens or
reproductive toxicants. The suit is in the discovery phase, and various procedural motions and defenses are being pursued. The Company believes that the suit is without merit, and the California
Attorney General has publicly stated that the case is without merit. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Environmental Matters</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
May&nbsp;2001, the State of Ohio notified the Company that it may be subject to an enforcement action for alleged past violations of the Company's wastewater discharge permit at its production
facility in Farmdale, Ohio. The State has offered to attempt to negotiate a settlement of this matter, and the Company has accepted the offer to do so. The State has not yet identified the relief it
may seek in this matter. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company is potentially liable for certain environmental matters arising from the operations of Nabisco's former wholly-owned subsidiary, Rowe Industries. Rowe operated a small engine manufacturing
facility in Sag Harbor, New York in the 1950s, 1960s and early 1970s that used various solvents. About 20 homes downgradient from the site were connected to public drinking water in the
mid-1980s after solvents were detected in their individual wells. Since 1996, three toxic tort cases have been brought against Nabisco in New York state court, collectively by or on behalf
of approximately 80 individuals, including 17 minors. The first case was filed on March&nbsp;6, 1996, in the Supreme Court of the State of New York and was subsequently dismissed by the trial court.
That decision was affirmed on appeal. The other two cases both were filed on January&nbsp;3, 2000, also in the Supreme Court of the State of New York. That court granted defendant's summary judgment
motion as to all but one of the plaintiffs in each of the remaining cases, and the plaintiffs have now withdrawn their appeal of this ruling. In August&nbsp;2002, the court entered summary judgment
against the remaining two plaintiffs. Plaintiffs have appealed this judgment, and the appeal is currently pending. </FONT></P>

</UL>

of the circumstances under which such statements were made, not misleading with respect to the period covered by this quarterly report;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>3.</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Based
on my knowledge, the financial statements, and other financial information included in this quarterly report, fairly present in all material respects the financial condition,
results of operations and cash flows of the registrant as of, and for, the periods presented in this quarterly report;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>4.</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>The
registrant's other certifying officers and I are responsible for establishing and maintaining disclosure controls and procedures (as defined in Exchange Act
Rules&nbsp;13a-14 and 15d-14) for the registrant and we have:

such disclosure controls and procedures to ensure that material information relating to the registrant, including its consolidated subsidiaries, is made known to us by others
within those entities, particularly during the period in which this quarterly report is being prepared;

the effectiveness of the registrant's disclosure controls and procedures as of a date within 90&nbsp;days prior to the filing date of this quarterly report (the "Evaluation
Date"); and
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>c)</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>presented
in this quarterly report our conclusions about the effectiveness of the disclosure controls and procedures based on our evaluation as of the Evaluation Date;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>5.</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>The
registrant's other certifying officers and I have disclosed, based on our most recent evaluation, to the registrant's auditors and the audit committee of registrant's board of
directors (or persons performing the equivalent function):
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>a)</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>all
significant deficiencies in the design or operation of internal controls which could adversely affect the registrant's ability to record, process, summarize and report financial
data and have identified for the registrant's auditors any material weaknesses in internal controls; and
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>b)</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>any
fraud, whether or not material, that involves management or other employees who have a significant role in the registrant's internal controls; and
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>6.</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>The
registrant's other certifying officers and I have indicated in this quarterly report whether or not there were significant changes in internal controls or in other factors that
could significantly affect internal controls subsequent to the date of our most recent evaluation, including any corrective actions with regard to significant deficiencies and material weaknesses. </FONT>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><B>5-YEAR REVOLVING CREDIT AGREEMENT  </B></FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><B> Dated as of July&nbsp;24, 2001  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;KRAFT FOODS&nbsp;INC., a Virginia corporation ("<U>Kraft</U>"), the banks, financial institutions and other institutional lenders (the
"<U>Initial Lenders</U>") listed on the signature pages hereof, and THE CHASE MANHATTAN BANK ("<U>Chase</U>") and CITIBANK, N.A.
("<U>Citibank</U>"), as administrative agents (each, in such capacity, an "<U>Administrative Agent</U>"), CREDIT SUISSE FIRST BOSTON and DEUTSCHE BANK AG
NEW YORK BRANCH AND/OR CAYMAN ISLANDS BRANCH ("<U>Deutsche Bank AG</U>"), as syndication agents (each, in such capacity, a "<U>Syndication Agent</U>") and
ABN AMRO BANK N.V., BNP PARIBAS, DRESDNER BANK AG, NEW YORK AND GRAND CAYMAN BRANCHES and HSBC BANK USA, as arrangers and documentation agents (each, in such capacity, an "<U>Arranger and
Documentation Agent</U>") for the Lenders (as hereinafter defined), agree as follows: </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>ARTICLE I </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>DEFINITIONS
AND ACCOUNTING TERMS </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Section&nbsp;1.01.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<U>Certain
Defined Terms.</U>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As used in this Agreement, the following terms shall have the following meanings (such
meanings to be equally applicable to both the singular and plural forms of the terms defined): </FONT></P>

<UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"<U>Advance</U>"
means a Pro Rata Advance or a Competitive Bid Advance. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"<U>Agents</U>"
means each Administrative Agent, each Syndication Agent and each Arranger and Documentation Agent. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"<U>Applicable
Facility Fee Rate</U>" means, for any period, a percentage per annum equal to the percentage set forth below determined by reference to the higher of
(i)&nbsp;the rating of Kraft's long-term senior unsecured Debt from Standard&nbsp;&amp; Poor's and (ii)&nbsp;the rating of Kraft's
long-term senior unsecured Debt from Moody's, in each case in effect from time to time during such period: </FONT></P>
</UL>

of Competitive Bid Borrowing</U>" has the meaning specified in Section&nbsp;2.07(b). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"<U>Notice
of Pro Rata Borrowing</U>" has the meaning specified in Section&nbsp;2.02(a). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"<U>Obligations</U>"
has the meaning specified in Section&nbsp;8.01. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"<U>Other
Taxes</U>" has the meaning specified in Section&nbsp;2.15(b). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"<U>Person</U>"
means an individual, partnership, corporation (including a business trust), joint stock company, trust, unincorporated association, joint venture,
limited liability company or other entity, or a government or any political subdivision or agency thereof. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"<U>Plan</U>"
means a Single Employer Plan or a Multiple Employer Plan. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"<U>Pro
Rata Advance</U>" means an advance by a Lender to any Borrower as part of a Pro Rata Borrowing and refers to a Base Rate Advance or a LIBO Rate Advance
(each of which shall be a "<U>Type</U>" of Pro Rata Advance). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"<U>Pro
Rata Borrowing</U>" means a borrowing consisting of simultaneous Pro Rata Advances of the same Type made by each of the Lenders pursuant to
Section&nbsp;2.01. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"<U>Pro
Rata Note</U>" means a promissory note of any Borrower payable to the order of any Lender, delivered pursuant to a request made under Section&nbsp;2.17 in
substantially the form of Exhibit&nbsp;A-1 hereto, evidencing the aggregate indebtedness of such Borrower to such Lender resulting from the Pro Rata Advances made by such Lender to such
Borrower. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"<U>Reference
Banks</U>" means Chase, Citibank, Credit Suisse First Boston and Deutsche Bank AG. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;"<U>Register</U>"
has the meaning specified in Section&nbsp;9.07(d). </FONT></P>

</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Section&nbsp;1.02.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<U>Computation
of Time Periods.</U>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In this Agreement in the computation of periods of time from a specified date to
a later specified date, the word "from" means "from and including" and the words "to" and "until" each mean "to but excluding". </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Section&nbsp;1.03.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<U>Accounting
Terms.</U>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;All accounting terms not specifically defined herein shall be construed in accordance with
accounting principles generally accepted in the United States, except that if there has
been a material change in an accounting principle affecting the definition of an accounting term as compared to that applied in the preparation of the financial statements of Kraft as of and for the
three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2001, then such new accounting principle shall not be used in the determination of the amount associated with that accounting term. A material change in an
accounting principle is one that, in the year of its adoption, changes the amount associated with the relevant accounting term for any quarter in such year by more than 10%. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>ARTICLE II </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>AMOUNTS
AND TERMS OF THE ADVANCES </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Section&nbsp;2.01.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<U>The
Pro Rata Advances.</U>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(a)&nbsp;<U>Obligation to Make Pro Rata
Advances.</U>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Each Lender severally agrees, on the terms and conditions hereinafter set forth, to make Pro Rata Advances to any Borrower from time to time on any Business Day
during the period from the Effective Date until the Termination Date in an aggregate amount not to exceed at any time outstanding such Lender's Commitment; <U>provided</U>,
<U>however</U>, that the aggregate amount of the Commitments of the Lenders shall be deemed used from time to time to the extent of the aggregate amount of the Competitive Bid
Advances then outstanding and such deemed use of the aggregate amount of the Commitments shall be allocated among the Lenders ratably according to their respective Commitments (such deemed use of the
aggregate amount of the Commitments being a "<U>Competitive Bid Reduction</U>"). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(b)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<U>Amount
of Pro Rata Borrowings.</U>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Each Pro Rata Borrowing shall be in an aggregate amount of no less than $50,000,000 or an
integral multiple of $1,000,000 in excess thereof. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(c)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<U>Type
of Pro Rata Advances.</U>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Each Pro Rata Borrowing shall consist of Pro Rata Advances of the same Type made on the same day by
the Lenders ratably according to their respective Commitments. Within the limits of each Lender's Commitment and subject to this Section&nbsp;2.01, any Borrower may borrow under this
Section&nbsp;2.01, prepay pursuant to Section&nbsp;2.11 or repay pursuant to Section&nbsp;2.03 and reborrow under this Section&nbsp;2.01. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Section&nbsp;2.02.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<U>Making
the Pro Rata Advances.</U>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(a)&nbsp;<U>Notice of Pro Rata
Borrowing.</U>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Each Pro Rata Borrowing shall be made on notice, given not later than (x)&nbsp;11:00&nbsp;A.M. (New York City time) on the third Business Day prior to the
date of the proposed Pro Rata Borrowing in the case of a Pro Rata Borrowing
consisting of LIBO Rate Advances, or (y)&nbsp;9:00&nbsp;A.M. (New York City time) on the date of the proposed Pro Rata Borrowing in the case of a Pro Rata Borrowing consisting of Base Rate
Advances, by the Borrower to Chase, as Administrative Agent, which shall give to each Lender prompt notice thereof by telecopier. Each such notice of a Pro Rata Borrowing (a "<U>Notice of
Pro Rata Borrowing</U>") shall be by telephone, confirmed immediately in writing, by registered mail or telecopier in substantially the form of Exhibit&nbsp;B-1 hereto,
specifying therein the requested: </FONT></P>

<UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(i)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;date
of such Pro Rata Borrowing, </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(ii)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Type
of Advances comprising such Pro Rata Borrowing, </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(iii)&nbsp;&nbsp;aggregate
amount of such Pro Rata Borrowing, and </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(iv)&nbsp;&nbsp;in
the case of a Pro Rata Borrowing consisting of LIBO Rate Advances, the initial Interest Period for each such Pro Rata Advance. Notwithstanding anything herein to the
contrary, no Borrower may select LIBO Rate Advances for any </FONT></P>

</UL>

<UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Pro
Rata Borrowing if the obligation of the Lenders to make LIBO Rate Advances shall then be suspended pursuant to Section&nbsp;2.08(c) or 2.13. </FONT></P>
